    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer10097821529571097254">Pat Conroy called Dorothea Benton Frank’s debut, <b>Sullivan’s Island</b>, “hilarious and wise,” while Anne Rivers Siddons declared that it “roars with life.” Now Frank evokes a lush plantation in the heart of modern-day South Carolina—where family ties and hidden truths run as deep and dark as the mighty Edisto River… Caroline Wimbley Levine always swore she’d never go home agai</span>
  <span id="freeText10097821529571097254" style="display:none">Pat Conroy called Dorothea Benton Frank’s debut, <b>Sullivan’s Island</b>, “hilarious and wise,” while Anne Rivers Siddons declared that it “roars with life.” Now Frank evokes a lush plantation in the heart of modern-day South Carolina—where family ties and hidden truths run as deep and dark as the mighty Edisto River… Caroline Wimbley Levine always swore she’d never go home again. But now, at her brother’s behest, she has returned to South Carolina to see about Mother—only to find that the years have not changed the Queen of Tall Pines Plantation. Miss Lavinia is as maddeningly eccentric as ever—and absolutely will not suffer the questionable advice of her children. This does not surprise Caroline. Nor does the fact that Tall Pines is still brimming with scandals and secrets, betrayals and lies. But she soon discovers that something is different this time around. It lies somewhere in the distance between her and her mother—and in her understanding of what it means to come home…</span>
  <a data-text-id="10097821529571097254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/569964-what-does-the-expression-yahn-mean-it">What does the expression &quot;yahn&quot; mean? It is used frequently in this book, and I have yet to be able to understand it.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_569964'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F65397.Plantation">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/569964-what-does-the-expression-yahn-mean-it">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/569964-what-does-the-expression-yahn-mean-it">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/5914556-jean-perry"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/5914556-jean-perry">Jean Perry</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's a southern colloquialism/contraction that takes the place of "hear" or "here" as used by non-southerners, usually as a question or command, as in<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's a southern colloquialism/contraction that takes the place of "hear" or "here" as used by non-southerners, usually as a question or command, as in "You be back by ten, y'ear?" I was surprised by the spelling Frank used. I would have spelled it "y'ear" or " ye'r". <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

<div id="review_236885135" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236885135" />
    <a title="Carolyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4269814-carolyn"><img alt="Carolyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1284072074p2/4269814.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/236885135?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/4269814-carolyn">Carolyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236885135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6972010118836723996">I've read several excellent novels set in the Low Country of the U.S. Southeast (roughly, along the tidal coast between Charleston and Savannah) by three authors: Pat Conroy, Anne Rivers Siddons, and Dorothea Benton Frank. Though a long way from being a native, I'm familiar with the territory because my husband grew up in Savannah and one of my brothers has lived in the Charleston area for 45 years or so. <br/><br/>As with the others, this book's characters are so richly drawn I felt as if I knew them as </span>
  <span id="freeText6972010118836723996" style="display:none">I've read several excellent novels set in the Low Country of the U.S. Southeast (roughly, along the tidal coast between Charleston and Savannah) by three authors: Pat Conroy, Anne Rivers Siddons, and Dorothea Benton Frank. Though a long way from being a native, I'm familiar with the territory because my husband grew up in Savannah and one of my brothers has lived in the Charleston area for 45 years or so. <br /><br />As with the others, this book's characters are so richly drawn I felt as if I knew them as well as members of my own family by the time I finished. They all have their problems and their character flaws, their moments of joy and grief. Most of them learn and grow. The plot is definitely secondary here. The story is mostly a family history, described sometimes by a mother, sometimes by her daughter, and sometimes by a neutral narrator. The land, the family, and the 19th century gracious home bind the characters with ties that are sometimes elastic, but almost unbreakable. <br /><br />I enjoyed the story very much and will definitely read more of Ms. Frank's sagas of the South. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6972010118836723996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kimberly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2669490-kimberly"><img alt="Kimberly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460135032p2/2669490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105579132?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kimberly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kimberly" href="/user/show/2669490-kimberly">Kimberly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669490-kimberly?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669490-kimberly?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105579132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8512017867000717387">The characters in Plantation are fantastic! Love them (Miss Lavinia) or not (Frances Mae), they are all vividly portrayed and intriguing. Certain characters reminded me so much of members of my own family, especially Trip's brood (I probably shouldn't say that, haha!). Frank's descriptions of the ACE Basin are so colorful and graphic you can feel the mugginess in the air, taste Miss Sweetie's strawberry jam, and smell Miss Lavinia's roses. This is one of the few books I've read that emotes both </span>
  <span id="freeText8512017867000717387" style="display:none">The characters in Plantation are fantastic! Love them (Miss Lavinia) or not (Frances Mae), they are all vividly portrayed and intriguing. Certain characters reminded me so much of members of my own family, especially Trip's brood (I probably shouldn't say that, haha!). Frank's descriptions of the ACE Basin are so colorful and graphic you can feel the mugginess in the air, taste Miss Sweetie's strawberry jam, and smell Miss Lavinia's roses. This is one of the few books I've read that emotes both humor and sorrow. As much as I enjoyed the story, it meandered a bit in parts for me; I felt as though it could have used some more editing. Still, I would rate it at 4.5 stars, rounded up to 5. I'm really looking forward to reading the sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7721416.Lowcountry_Summer_A_Plantation_Novel" title="Lowcountry Summer A Plantation Novel by Dorothea Benton Frank" rel="nofollow noopener">Lowcountry Summer: A Plantation Novel</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8512017867000717387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_207215509" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/207215509" />
    <a title="JudiAnne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1266107-judianne"><img alt="JudiAnne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573326593p2/1266107.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/207215509?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JudiAnne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JudiAnne" href="/user/show/1266107-judianne">JudiAnne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer207215509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17731582151272604704">I picked this novel up at a local library book sale for 25 cents and I got a big surprise when I opened the book and started reading. I couldn't stop turning the pages of this mesmerizing story of a family in distress in the Low Country, which are the islands surrounding Charleston, SC. As I was reading this wonderful novel I couldn't help thinking the the writing style seemed similar to a cross between Pat Conroy and Fannie Flag, two popular southern authors. This novel will be a revisit for an</span>
  <span id="freeText17731582151272604704" style="display:none">I picked this novel up at a local library book sale for 25 cents and I got a big surprise when I opened the book and started reading. I couldn't stop turning the pages of this mesmerizing story of a family in distress in the Low Country, which are the islands surrounding Charleston, SC. As I was reading this wonderful novel I couldn't help thinking the the writing style seemed similar to a cross between Pat Conroy and Fannie Flag, two popular southern authors. This novel will be a revisit for anyone who has been to the shores of South Carolina and for anyone who has not, I will bet that you will make plans to visit soon after reading this smart and sassy tale of the shores of the Low Country. Also, the language is right on for that area. I only say this because I read a comment where a reviewer asks the question, "Who talks like that"? <br /><br />From page one you know that the matriarch of the family, Lavinia has died since the prologue starts out with her funeral. From the first chapter the story goes back a few months and brings you up to that time. During this time you will get to know and love the characters of the dysfunctional Wimbly family and their friends. "Plantation" is such an emotional roller coaster that I promise they will keep you smiling, laughing out loud and boo hooing like a baby. <br /><br />Caroline Wimbly has fled to New York City to get away from her mother and the Low Country. She marries and has a son who has learning disabilities. When her disastrous marriage falls apart, she and her son flee NYC to return to her home where she feels safe. Even though her brother is in financial trouble, and his wife is a loose tongued, mean spirited piece of trash she begins to feel as though she has really come home. In light of all of this and while she is in the mist of several other colorful characters, she finds comfort in the arms of her cantankerous but larger than life mother and her surrogate mother, Millie, the housekeeper. Caroline begins a journey of new found love of family and her very own Low Country of South Carolina. As, they say in the south, "It's a hoot, ya heah?"<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17731582151272604704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo"><img alt="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448623481p2/3615945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/723998177?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" href="/user/show/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo">Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=good-fiction">good-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=permanent-library">permanent-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=fall-2013">fall-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=womens-fiction">womens-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer723998177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17428803958373059929">I love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/36935.Dorothea_Benton_Frank' title='Dorothea Benton Frank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dorothea Benton Frank</a>. She always writes wonderful stories with very strong women characters and Plantation is no exception. Millie is wonderful with her fiery personality and her Gullah dialect and her potions. She is a great sidekick to Miss Lavinia, the Queen of Tall Pines. Miss Lavinia is eccentric as they come. She rules her little world with a strict discipline - Miss Manners must be proud. She is irreverent. She is funny. She is warm when she wants to be. And she loves to have fun </span>
  <span id="freeText17428803958373059929" style="display:none">I love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/36935.Dorothea_Benton_Frank" title="Dorothea Benton Frank" rel="nofollow noopener">Dorothea Benton Frank</a>. She always writes wonderful stories with very strong women characters and Plantation is no exception. Millie is wonderful with her fiery personality and her Gullah dialect and her potions. She is a great sidekick to Miss Lavinia, the Queen of Tall Pines. Miss Lavinia is eccentric as they come. She rules her little world with a strict discipline - Miss Manners must be proud. She is irreverent. She is funny. She is warm when she wants to be. And she loves to have fun and loves her men. And she is dying. It is at an inopportune time - she is just discovering her two children, Trip and Caroline and her grandson, Eric.<br /> <br />Caroline Wimbley Levine has returned to Tall Pines to see about Mother. That is what she tells herself. Miss Lavinia could not be "off her rocker," could she? There is more to Trip's story that meets the eye - why does he need money so frequently and more importantly why does he want to remove Miss Lavinia from her throne at Tall Pines? Her marriage to Richard is shaky - good gawd girl, what were ya thinkin'!?! <i>Plantation</i> is Caroline's and Lavinia's stories in the last months of the Queen of Tall Pines' life. It is the story in which Caroline becomes Miss Caroline of Tall Pines with Miss Lavinia, Millie, Miss Sweetie, and Miss Nancy all helping. <br /> <br />But I only have one complaint about this delicious book - Frances Mae! What a work she is - an always pregnant piece of redneck trailer park white trash! Ohhhhhhh my Southern is showing! </span>
  <a data-text-id="17428803958373059929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2011337439" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2011337439" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2472822-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481521329p2/2472822.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2011337439?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/2472822-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2011337439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4695292136065472401">Lord, I love this woman's writing. If you are looking for fast-paced excitement and steamy sex, buy a different book. But if you want to sink into a slow, sensuous taste of the deep South, with all its traditions, its failings, and its triumphs, if you want to feel the low, sleepy waters of the Low Country move like warm honey through your veins, then Plantation will take you there in style. ALL of Dorothea Benton Franks books that I have read to date (and I am sadly behind) leave me wanting to </span>
  <span id="freeText4695292136065472401" style="display:none">Lord, I love this woman's writing. If you are looking for fast-paced excitement and steamy sex, buy a different book. But if you want to sink into a slow, sensuous taste of the deep South, with all its traditions, its failings, and its triumphs, if you want to feel the low, sleepy waters of the Low Country move like warm honey through your veins, then Plantation will take you there in style. ALL of Dorothea Benton Franks books that I have read to date (and I am sadly behind) leave me wanting to sip mimosas in the shade of a magnolia tree next to a lazy river. <br /><br />Don't worry about reading the Low Country Tales in order. This is a "series" connected by geography, not plot line or characters. Grab the first one you see, find a comfy spot to settle in for a while, take a deep breath and relax.</span>

          </span>

    <a title="Susan Serra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51820165-susan-serra"><img alt="Susan Serra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453464998p2/51820165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2817297050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5729128470471673590">This is my third Dorothea Frank novel. Just love all of them. So much fun to read, and her characterizations are WONDERFUL! You can truly immerse yourself within this story. Now, for those of you who know me know that I am a New England girl through and through. But, I LOVE these novels. Don't be afraid to read them out of sequence, as each stands on its own. This story involves daughter who has left her Lowcountry world behind for a fabulous marriage and life in New York, or so she thought. Ms.</span>
  <span id="freeText5729128470471673590" style="display:none">This is my third Dorothea Frank novel. Just love all of them. So much fun to read, and her characterizations are WONDERFUL! You can truly immerse yourself within this story. Now, for those of you who know me know that I am a New England girl through and through. But, I LOVE these novels. Don't be afraid to read them out of sequence, as each stands on its own. This story involves daughter who has left her Lowcountry world behind for a fabulous marriage and life in New York, or so she thought. Ms. Lavinia, the plantation owner of Tall Pines, remains, and although eccentric in many ways, loving her family and staff completely. You will love the characters, all of them, for they are amazing, each in their own way. I just love the way she writes. You will find diversity in the opinions of Frank's writing. Most love, but many do not love her writing. I hope you will as I do!</span>

          </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6146598655640907585">Plantation by Dorothea Benton Frank has been on the "gotta get to this book" list for some time. Now that a follow-up book, Lowcountry Summer, has just come out, I figured it was time to get to Plantation which I had downloaded to my Kindle last year.<br/><br/>Plantation was a story of a family finding its true self again after years of misinterpretations and misunderstandings. I enjoyed seeing Caroline Wimbley Levine find her true heart and home, although it seemed at times that she certainly was taking </span>
  <span id="freeText6146598655640907585" style="display:none">Plantation by Dorothea Benton Frank has been on the "gotta get to this book" list for some time. Now that a follow-up book, Lowcountry Summer, has just come out, I figured it was time to get to Plantation which I had downloaded to my Kindle last year.<br /><br />Plantation was a story of a family finding its true self again after years of misinterpretations and misunderstandings. I enjoyed seeing Caroline Wimbley Levine find her true heart and home, although it seemed at times that she certainly was taking a lot of needless side trips along the way. I have put Lowcountry Summer on my library reserve list; however, I see from many reviews that this follow-up to Plantation is getting some of the same bad reviews as did Return to Sullivan's Island. Sometimes, unless it is clear that the author set out to write a series, characters may be best served by our remembering them as we last knew them in print or as we, the readers, chose to imagine what happened next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6146598655640907585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1205793797587667620">I really enjoyed reading this book, until the end; not that the ending was bad...I just don't care for sad endings.   <span id="freeText1205793797587667620" style="display:none">I really enjoyed reading this book, until the end; not that the ending was bad...I just don't care for sad endings. The whole book tended to be on the humorous side but the ending took a turn for the serious that didn't really mesh with the tone of the rest of the book. <br /><br />The main character, Caroline, deals with major life changes with a quick wit and sassy southern charm. She grows up idolizing her father who was taken away from the family far too early. Caroline is left with her brother while her mother falls apart with the loss of her beloved partner in life. These details might have been more helpful towards the beginning of the book, rather than in the middle, as to explain Caroline's reluctance at returning to Tall Pine to lick her wounds. <br /><br />You will cheer for Caroline and the Wimbley's all the way through till the end. This book doesn't disappoint, but falls a bit short at the end for me. </span>

<div id="review_400204075" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/400204075" />
    <a title="Alyce Joines" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1434147-alyce-joines"><img alt="Alyce Joines" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251922530p2/1434147.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/400204075?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyce Joines" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyce Joines" href="/user/show/1434147-alyce-joines">Alyce Joines</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer400204075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14879556474988538828">An "eyes wide open" look at mother-daughter relationships, <i>Plantation</i> introduces us to Caroline Wimbley Levine who left her southern home for the big city, married and had a son. She also left behind her mother, Miss Lavinia, and her brother, Trip. Caroline comes back to the plantation after both call her with wildly varying stories of an incident in which Miss Lavinia fired a gun at Trip. Finding the truth behind this story and many others which Caroline had believed since she was a child gives</span>
  <span id="freeText14879556474988538828" style="display:none">An "eyes wide open" look at mother-daughter relationships, <i>Plantation</i> introduces us to Caroline Wimbley Levine who left her southern home for the big city, married and had a son. She also left behind her mother, Miss Lavinia, and her brother, Trip. Caroline comes back to the plantation after both call her with wildly varying stories of an incident in which Miss Lavinia fired a gun at Trip. Finding the truth behind this story and many others which Caroline had believed since she was a child gives her a new perspective on her family and the plantation which her ancestors built. The book is a slow roller-coaster ride of emotions, long but quickly read, a good choice as a summer beach book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14879556474988538828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40080773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13047433512830592343">A masterpiece in what I would call "character-driven fiction." Much like my own writing, it's not the plot-points that sell this as much as the characters, think Fanny Flagg but faster moving fiction. The mother in this novel is one of the best female characters I've seen in a long time and quite original, warm, funny, inviting. It's told from the daughter's point of view in first person. You will bawl your eyes out towards the end when the mother holds her last great "Hurrah!" in her pontoon bo</span>
  <span id="freeText13047433512830592343" style="display:none">A masterpiece in what I would call "character-driven fiction." Much like my own writing, it's not the plot-points that sell this as much as the characters, think Fanny Flagg but faster moving fiction. The mother in this novel is one of the best female characters I've seen in a long time and quite original, warm, funny, inviting. It's told from the daughter's point of view in first person. You will bawl your eyes out towards the end when the mother holds her last great "Hurrah!" in her pontoon boat on the river. It's the best work by this author, and I plan on reading it again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13047433512830592343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1071067926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13149654532352901860">I guess I'd rate this one at 3.5. I liked it better than Sullivan's Island because I felt the story progressed a bit better. I am finding an unlikely amount of love interests in her stories. It seems that every man these women meet just about fall in love with them and no one ever really seems angry when the romance fizzles. And they are always so friendly with each other. No hurt feelings or jealousy. Seems a bit unrealistic to me, but it was a cute, feel good story none-the-less.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10820124312197184339">I might finish this book at some point, but 200 pages in and I'm going to start something else. I didn't realize it was part of a series, but I don't think I would like it any more if I had started with book 1. I don't like the breezy and artificial writing style and I just don't care about the characters, the story, or even the NY vs southern plantation setting. This one is going back to the donation bin for the next book sale. Perhaps its next reader will enjoy it more than I did.</span>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer181467100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6226811027813396741">I loved Frank's Sullivan Island so I thought I would love this one too. I picked up and put it down, picked it up and put it down. Then last week I picked it up again and finished it in two days. I love the southern humor and the voodoo herbs. This is a fun read once you get past the first couple of chapters it swings into gear and you'll be laughing all the way to the end. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer334728278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1339111993423975648">I should have read this one first, but I accidently read Lowcountry Summer first (which is the continuing story of the Wimbley family.) I love Miss Lavinia, owner of the plantation. She is an exact copy of my mother-in-law! Perfect manners, everything served in just the right way, with the perfect linens, dishes, and goblets. Lots of humor and sarcasm galore.</span>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1533691148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer149198192467952953">I loved this book so much. The setting was beautiful, the characters were awesome (you either love them or love to hate them), loads of good family drama and a touch of romance. Miss Lavinia will make you laugh out loud. My favorite DB Frank book so far, but I've got a lot of her books to go yet. One of my very favorite authors. </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cvaSvKcz+J74Rc0PYX5lCgSzYHhblJHEoajCyCFtpB8CN7MU9fR9Kp5x/j2Qh1rBhgcz6Mm3oHD6sT7GPY+Qow==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RBcru14TlJ8SS+Fl8zD1QCtj3J66bM5oTDkvTm2EGr801goTDNQRK3R/0lcCycqLqdePDihP/9wXINNAcWYuAw==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_49931119'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49931119-on-ocean-boulevard?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">On Ocean Boulevard<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/5080.Mary_Alice_Monroe?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Mary Alice Monroe<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.10 avg rating &mdash; 4,678 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2020\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer7299150163248875772\">The New York Times bestselling author of The Summer Guests returns at long last to her beloved Beach House series in this breathtaking novel about one family’s summer of forging new beginnings against the enduring beauty and resilience of the natural<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText7299150163248875772\" style=\"display:none\">The New York Times bestselling author of The Summer Guests returns at long last to her beloved Beach House series in this breathtaking novel about one family’s summer of forging new beginnings against the enduring beauty and resilience of the natural world.\n\nIt’s been sixteen years since Caretta “Cara” Rutledge has returned home to the beautiful shores of Charleston, South Carolina. Over those years, she has weathered the tides of deaths and births, struggles and joys. And now, as Cara prepares for her second wedding, her life is about to change yet again.\n\nMeanwhile, the rest of the storied Rutledge family is also in flux. Cara’s niece Linnea returns to Sullivan’s Island to begin a new career and an unexpected relationship. Linnea’s parents, having survived bankruptcy, pin their hopes and futures on the construction of a new home on Ocean Boulevard. But as excitement over the house and wedding builds, a devastating illness strikes the family and brings plans to a screeching halt. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/36935.Dorothea_Benton_Frank">Dorothea Benton Frank
</a></div>

4,115
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7488028056498695101">Dorothea Benton Frank was a <i>New York Times</i> best-selling American novelist of Southern fiction. She worked in the apparel industry from 1972 until 1985 and then organized fundraisers as a volunteer, before becoming a novelist.<br/><br/>She is best known as the author of twenty novels placed in and around the Lowcountry of South Carolina. </span>

</div>

The oldest, Lindsey, who always held her younger sister in check, is leaving for college. And Gracie, her Tasmanian devil, is giving her nightmares. Linda’s personal life? Well, between the married men, the cold New Jersey winters, her pinched wallet and her ex-husband who marries a beautiful, successful woman ten years younger than she is—let’s just say, Linda has seen enough to fill a thousand pages.\n\nAs the story opens, she is barreling down Interstate 95, bound for Mount Pleasant, South Carolina, the land of her ancestors. Welcomed by the generous heart of her advice dispensing sister, Mimi, Linda and her daughters slowly begin to find their way and discover a sweeter rhythm of life.\n\nAnd then there’s Brad Jackson, a former investment banker of Atlanta, Georgia who hires her to run his restaurant on Shem Creek. Like everyone else, Brad’s got a story of his own—namely an almost ex-wife, Loretta who is the kind of gal who gives women a bad name.\n\nThe real protagonist of this story is the Lowcountry itself. The magical waters of Shem Creek, the abundant wildlife and the astounding power of nature give this tiny corner of the planet its infallible reputation as a place for introspection, contemplation and healing.\n\nAs in all her previous work, you’ll find Shem Creek to be compulsively readable, irreverent but warm and blazingly authentic—and you’ll dread reaching the last page. It is her vivid writing, colorful characters and rich narrative that have made Dorothea Benton Frank one of our nation’s greatest storytellers. Shem Creek is a triumphant novel that proves we are all entitled to a second chance. As Adam and Eve get caught up on their lives, their partners strike up a deep friendship—and flirt with an unexpected attraction—of their own.\n\nYear after year, Adam, Eliza, Eve, and Carl eagerly await their reunion at Wild Dunes, a condominium complex at the island’s tip end, where they grow closer with each passing day, building a friendship that will withstand financial catastrophe, family tragedy, and devastating heartbreak.
